This also allows the use of <a href="/wiki/Electroporation" title="Electroporation">electroporation</a> for studying the effect of adding or silencing a gene. Other tools for perturbing their genetic makeup are chicken <a href="/wiki/Embryonic_stem_cell" title="Embryonic stem cell">embryonic stem cells</a> and <a href="/wiki/Viral_vector" title="Viral vector">viral vectors</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">&#91;95&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Collaborative_studies">Collaborative studies</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ornithology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Collaborative studies">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:CanadaGooseSummer19942003.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/CanadaGooseSummer19942003.png/220px-CanadaGooseSummer19942003.png" width="220" height="170" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/CanadaGooseSummer19942003.png/330px-CanadaGooseSummer19942003.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/CanadaGooseSummer19942003.png/440px-CanadaGooseSummer19942003.png 2x" data-file-width="578" data-file-height="447" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:CanadaGooseSummer19942003.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Summer distribution and abundance of <a href="/wiki/Canada_goose" title="Canada goose">Canada goose</a> using data from the North American Breeding Bird Surveys 1994\xe2\x80\x932003</div></div></div>\n<p>With the widespread interest in birds,  use of a large number of people to work on collaborative ornithological projects that cover large geographic scales has been possible.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">&#91;96&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">&#91;97&#93;</a></sup> These <a href="/wiki/Citizen_science" title="Citizen science">citizen science</a> projects include nationwide projects such as the <a href="/wiki/Christmas_Bird_Count" title="Christmas Bird Count">Christmas Bird Count</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-98" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-98">&#91;98&#93;</a></sup> Backyard Bird Count,<sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">&#91;99&#93;</a></sup> the North American <a href="/wiki/Breeding_Bird_Survey" class="mw-redirect" title="Breeding Bird Survey">Breeding Bird Survey</a>, the Canadian EPOQ<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">&#91;100&#93;</a></sup> or regional projects such as the Asian Waterfowl Census and <a rel="nofollow" class="external text" href="http://www.springalive.net/world">Spring Alive</a> in Europe. These projects help to identify distributions of birds, their population densities and changes over time, arrival and departure dates of migration, breeding seasonality, and even population genetics.<sup id="cite_ref-101" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-101">&#91;101&#93;</a></sup> The results of many of these projects are published as <a href="/wiki/Bird_atlas" title="Bird atlas">bird atlases</a>. Studies of migration using bird ringing or colour marking often involve the cooperation of people and organizations in different countries.<sup id="cite_ref-102" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-102">&#91;102&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">Applications</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ornithology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Applications">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Bird_strike" title="Bird strike">Bird strike</a> and <a href="/wiki/Bird_conservation" title="Bird conservation">Bird conservation</a></div>\n<p>Wild birds impact many human activities, while domesticated birds are important sources of eggs, meat, feathers, and other products. Applied and economic ornithology aim to reduce the ill effects of problem birds and enhance gains from beneficial species.\n</p>\n<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a href="/wiki/File:Red-billed_quelea_flocking_at_waterhole.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Red-billed_quelea_flocking_at_waterhole.jpg/220px-Red-billed_quelea_flocking_at_waterhole.jpg" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Red-billed_quelea_flocking_at_waterhole.jpg/330px-Red-billed_quelea_flocking_at_waterhole.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/9/95/Red-billed_quelea_flocking_at_waterhole.jpg/440px-Red-billed_quelea_flocking_at_waterhole.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1600" data-file-height="1200" /></a>  <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a href="/wiki/File:Red-billed_quelea_flocking_at_waterhole.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a></div><a href="/wiki/Red-billed_quelea" title="Red-billed quelea">Red-billed queleas</a> are a major agricultural pest in parts of Africa.</div></div></div>\n<p>The role of some species of birds as <a href="/wiki/Pest_(organism)" title="Pest (organism)">pests</a> has been well known, particularly in agriculture. <a href="/wiki/Seed_predation" title="Seed predation">Granivorous</a> birds such as the <a href="/wiki/Quelea" title="Quelea">queleas</a> in Africa are among the most numerous birds in the world, and foraging flocks can cause devastation.<sup id="cite_ref-103" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-103">&#91;103&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-104" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-104">&#91;104&#93;</a></sup> Many insectivorous birds are also noted as beneficial in agriculture. Many early studies on the benefits or damages caused by birds in fields were made by analysis of stomach contents and observation of feeding behaviour.<sup id="cite_ref-105" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-105">&#91;105&#93;</a></sup> Modern studies aimed to manage birds in agriculture make use of a wide range of principles from ecology.<sup id="cite_ref-106" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-106">&#91;106&#93;</a></sup> Intensive <a href="/wiki/Aquaculture" title="Aquaculture">aquaculture</a> has brought humans in conflict with fish-eating birds such as <a href="/wiki/Cormorant" title="Cormorant">cormorants</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-107" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-107">&#91;107&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Large flocks of pigeons and starlings in cities are often considered as a nuisance, and techniques to reduce their populations or their impacts are constantly innovated.<sup id="cite_ref-108" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-108">&#91;108&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-109" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-109">&#91;109&#93;</a></sup> Birds are also of medical importance, and their role as carriers of human diseases such as <a href="/wiki/Japanese_encephalitis" title="Japanese encephalitis">Japanese encephalitis</a>, <a href="/wiki/West_Nile_virus" title="West Nile virus">West Nile virus</a>, and influenza <a href="/wiki/H5N1" class="mw-redirect" title="H5N1">H5N1</a> have been widely recognised.<sup id="cite_ref-110" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-110">&#91;110&#93;</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-111" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-111">&#91;111&#93;</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Bird_strike" title="Bird strike">Bird strikes</a> and the damage they cause in <a href="/wiki/Aviation" title="Aviation">aviation</a> are of particularly great importance, due to the fatal consequences and the level of economic losses caused. The airline industry incurs worldwide damages of an estimated US$1.2 billion each year.<sup id="cite_ref-112" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-112">&#91;112&#93;</a></sup>\n</p><p>Many species of birds have been driven to <a href="/wiki/List_of_extinct_birds" class="mw-redirect" title="List of extinct birds">extinction</a> by human activities. Being conspicuous elements of the ecosystem, they have been considered as indicators of ecological health.<sup id="cite_ref-113" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-113">&#91;113&#93;</a></sup> They have also helped in gathering support for <a href="/wiki/Habitat_conservation" title="Habitat conservation">habitat conservation</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-114" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-114">&#91;114&#93;</a></sup> Bird conservation requires specialized knowledge in aspects of biology and ecology, and may require the use of very location-specific approaches. Ornithologists contribute to <a href="/wiki/Conservation_biology" title="Conservation biology">conservation biology</a> by studying the ecology of birds in the wild and identifying the key threats and ways of enhancing the survival of species.<sup id="cite_ref-115" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-115">&#91;115&#93;</a></sup> Critically endangered species such as the California condor have had to be captured and bred in captivity. Such <a href="/wiki/Ex-situ_conservation" class="mw-redirect" title="Ex-situ conservation"><i>ex situ</i> conservation</a> measures may be followed by reintroduction of the species into the wild.<sup id="cite_ref-116" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-116">&#91;116&#93;</a></sup>\n</p>\n<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Ornithology&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>\n<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Avian_ecology_field_methods" title="Avian ecology field methods">Avian ecology field methods</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/Bird_observatory" title="Bird observatory">Bird observatory</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_ornithologists" title="List of ornithologists">List of ornithologists</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_ornithologists_abbreviated_names" title="List of ornithologists abbreviated names">List of ornithologists abbreviated names</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_ornithological_societies" title="List of ornithological societies">List of ornithological societies</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_ornithology_journals" title="List of ornithology journals">List of ornithology journals</a></li>\n<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_ornithology_awards" title="List of ornithology awards">List of ornithology awards</a></li></ul>\n<h2><span
